<div id="review_1260474437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1260474437" />
    <a title="S.H. Villa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23335286-s-h-villa"><img alt="S.H. Villa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429451435p2/23335286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260474437?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.H. Villa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.H. Villa" href="/user/show/23335286-s-h-villa">S.H. Villa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260474437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10859707021938772740">It took over a millenia for the Catholic Church to be seen through. They must have had a good press officer. But see through it they did. Luther wasn't the first, but he certainly hit the headlines when he nailed his 95 theses to the church door in Wittenburg. <br/><br/>Basically, Q is a war story. Which quickly moved from a war about ideologies to a class war, the same class war that underlay and still underlies nearly all of human history. Our superhero, the man of many names, moves through the storm wh</span>
  <span id="freeText10859707021938772740" style="display:none">It took over a millenia for the Catholic Church to be seen through. They must have had a good press officer. But see through it they did. Luther wasn't the first, but he certainly hit the headlines when he nailed his 95 theses to the church door in Wittenburg. <br /><br />Basically, Q is a war story. Which quickly moved from a war about ideologies to a class war, the same class war that underlay and still underlies nearly all of human history. Our superhero, the man of many names, moves through the storm which hit Europe at that time, telling us the tale of many defeats. Meanwhile, our superspy, Q, reports to Rome and manipulates the peasantry to their own destruction. Each version of protestantism becomes increasingly more autonomous until we arrive at Anabaptism, where the community regulates itself without state or religious interference. A very dangerous idea which is still being put about today by those such as the Indignados in Spain and the Occupy Movement in the US and elsewhere. Not to mention Alexis Tsiripas in Greece, the David facing up to the Goliath of the IMF and the European Central Bank giants. <br /><br />After reading Q, I read Norman Lewis's The Honoured Society about the mafia in Sicily. Same story. The ruling class (consisting of church, landowners and mafia) manipulate others such as the bandits to keep Sicily in a suspended state of feudalism.<br /><br />I had previously read Manser's NATO's Secret Armies about the false flag operations in Europe after the war to discredit communism. I followed this up with The Lone Gladio by Sibel Edmonds who shows us how those false flag operations were continued, including the big one - 9/11 itself. The CIA continues to finance and arm the so-called Muslim fundamentalists to keep the war fresh and in the headlines, allowing them to justify armed intervention, drones, genocide and good ol' tried and true rape &amp; pillage.<br /><br />There is a strong sense of history repeating itself. Q is a good place to start, but don't stop there, because the class war is still on and we're losing at the moment. As we have been throughout 99% of history.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10859707021938772740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307500815?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt Gough" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt Gough" href="/user/show/8620410-matt-gough">Matt Gough</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307500815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7065078369590747293">This book had a lot of potential. It was about the Reformation and followed one man as he moved across Europe, starting in Germany, moving to Holland, and ending up in Italy. The man was trying to keep the Reformation alive and constantly sought followers wherever he went. He was dogged by a man named “Q,” who was working for a Cardinal interested in keeping Catholicism dominant over Europe. It was a great premise and parts of it were interesting, but the execution was not as well done as it sho</span>
  <span id="freeText7065078369590747293" style="display:none">This book had a lot of potential. It was about the Reformation and followed one man as he moved across Europe, starting in Germany, moving to Holland, and ending up in Italy. The man was trying to keep the Reformation alive and constantly sought followers wherever he went. He was dogged by a man named “Q,” who was working for a Cardinal interested in keeping Catholicism dominant over Europe. It was a great premise and parts of it were interesting, but the execution was not as well done as it should have been. The style was sloppy, which can’t entirely be blamed on the fact that it was translated from Italian. And I found out that the anonymous authors are all Communists and put their rhetoric into their books, which I could see in Q, so that turned me off a bit, too. A good premise, but ultimately not worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7065078369590747293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4869843067991530313" style="display:none">A harsh novel set during the Reformation. It was written by a group of Italian Leftists under a pseudonym. An epic if i've ever read one. I did some reading about John of Leiden and i don't think he was ever a pimp in the old usage of the word). A little harsh as far as language and imagery but i suppose this was an extremely harsh time to live in. The first Marxist treatment of the Reformation ive ever been exposed too. Something for Liberation theologians to look into. </span>

<div id="review_43222461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43222461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12297277826932205614">This curious product of a shady Italian anarchist collective, named after an ex-Bournemouth, Watford and AC Milan striker intrigued me to such a degrree that I promptly took a holiday in Germany on the back of it. The image of the cage hanging from Munster Cathedral, with its bones of the executed Anabaptists, is one of the strongest images from an incredible novel - one that covers over a hundred years of the history of the reformation with amazing aplomb.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_216325633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/216325633" />
    <a title="Edward Creter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4665308-edward-creter"><img alt="Edward Creter" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/216325633?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Creter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Creter" href="/user/show/4665308-edward-creter">Edward Creter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=latino-culture">latino-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=raiders-esque-action-adventure">raiders-esque-action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=world-travel">world-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=controversial-literature">controversial-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=titles-the-q-105s">titles-the-q-105s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=chunky-books">chunky-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665308-edward-creter?shelf=historical-novels">historical-novels</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer216325633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16489326992938097393">Q s an eye-opener for me as a Christian, and normally I wouldn't read something as Christian bashing as, say, DaVinci Code, etc., but this book is about world history and the religious wars that took place in the Medieval European period, so anything anti-Christian is easy to overlook, maybe even forgive! (?) It's 16-century Germany, and a humble priest named Gert is challenged by letters from a mysterious man known only as Q to reshape history--if he can! He must endure religious hardships as t</span>
  <span id="freeText16489326992938097393" style="display:none">Q s an eye-opener for me as a Christian, and normally I wouldn't read something as Christian bashing as, say, DaVinci Code, etc., but this book is about world history and the religious wars that took place in the Medieval European period, so anything anti-Christian is easy to overlook, maybe even forgive! (?) It's 16-century Germany, and a humble priest named Gert is challenged by letters from a mysterious man known only as Q to reshape history--if he can! He must endure religious hardships as the Catholics wage unholy war against the Protestants ("unholy war" is a mild way of putting it.) and deliver a book about the compassion of Christ that will shake the mores of civilization, anger the Catholics and change the world forever...something the Pope is unpleased about! This novel was actually written by four writers in Italy who went under one name, Luther Blissett...so NO ONE WILL EVER KNOW!!! And it does have mega-violence, fine-arts style nudity and enough language to make Andrew Dice Clay cringe, but it also is honest in its portrayal of religious wars and prejudice--the stigma of which still resonates with all of us today. It has my Seal of Approval for readers of controversial books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16489326992938097393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1222114031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222114031" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26789252-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429755396p2/26789252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1222114031?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/26789252-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780151010639" href="/book/show/1077048.Q">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26789252-chris?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1222114031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10000985840407800309">That was quite good. At first I was really excited because GoodReads recommended it to me because I liked Umberto Eco's books, then I did some reading about the author and started wondering if this was some kind of communist screed (it's not) and then I actually read it and was engrossed.<br/><br/>Our hero (who has set aside his birth name long ago) is a part of the Reformation trying to establish Baptist communes and enclaves in northern Germany and the low countries. Along the way the Baptists are conti</span>
  <span id="freeText10000985840407800309" style="display:none">That was quite good. At first I was really excited because GoodReads recommended it to me because I liked Umberto Eco's books, then I did some reading about the author and started wondering if this was some kind of communist screed (it's not) and then I actually read it and was engrossed.<br /><br />Our hero (who has set aside his birth name long ago) is a part of the Reformation trying to establish Baptist communes and enclaves in northern Germany and the low countries. Along the way the Baptists are continually hunted by pro Catholic and pro Lutheran forces seeking to enforce obedience to the local sovereign. In particular, the eponymous Q who proves to be the most deadly enemy of the reformers.<br /><br />And that's the story, we follow the main character as he tries and struggles to spread his new sect throughout Europe, trying to dodge the Inquisition and support the moderate elements of the Catholic Church. All the while being tracked by Q. It's at parts exciting, brutal, beautiful and melancholy.<br /><br />And now I'm off to look up some of the characters in this book to find out how many of them really existed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10000985840407800309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y9ei41epd7yszKPa/lvciR1FvtKmZxs+4q7ge13T3K9ajhA/fQr3Xs7tjXSnbXX+fkiwTEcEwA2cwxXERBsk8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rGwPL0An6GTPTzKsq1hIZHQ4aWH2EraYTlYRw1Tgd1+VNb3zaoRohq1uHALybuETFzVn/xdxbaswO+R8TSiPAA==')})
  }

Called in to investigate, melancholy Detective Ciccio, a secret admirer of the murdered woman and a friend of her husband’s, discovers that almost everyone in the apartment building is somehow involved in the case, and with each new development the mystery only deepens and broadens. Gadda’s sublimely different detective story presents a scathing picture of fascist Italy while tracking the elusiveness of the truth, the impossibility of proof, and the infinite complexity of the workings of fate, showing how they come into conflict with the demands of justice and love. Italo Calvino, Pier Paolo Pasolini, and Alberto Moravia all considered That Awful Mess on the Via Merulana to be the great modern Italian novel. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17535239558509083911">Luther Blissett is a "multiple name" adopted by many people all over the world since the mid-1990s, as part of a transnational activist project. This practice started in Italy when a vast network of cultural workers "borrowed" the name of a Jamaica born soccer player active in England and in Italy in the previous decade. Later on, the name was used as a collective pen name by a group of four Itali</span>
  <span id="freeText17535239558509083911" style="display:none">Luther Blissett is a "multiple name" adopted by many people all over the world since the mid-1990s, as part of a transnational activist project. This practice started in Italy when a vast network of cultural workers "borrowed" the name of a Jamaica born soccer player active in England and in Italy in the previous decade. Later on, the name was used as a collective pen name by a group of four Italian writers: Roberto Bui, Giovanni Cattabriga, Federico Guglielmi and Luca Di Meo, authors of the novel "Q". Since January 2000, however, they have been writing under another collective pen name: Wu Ming (aka "Wu Ming Foundation").<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/191397.Wu_Ming">http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17535239558509083911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
